Movie Special

Overseas News

New Life in Hollywood: Stars Make a Big Fuss Over Babies

— Mei Cun

In the past, everyone knew that Hollywood stars competed and flaunted their wealth in terms of clothing, food, housing, and entertainment. But there has never been such a craze for children as there is now. In the past, their weapons against each other were dazzling clothes, luxurious cars, extravagant banquets, and magnificent mansions. Even in terms of entertainment, one built a nine-hole golf course, and others competed to build eighteen-hole courses. After William Hayes laid a carpet covered with various patterns of Earth in the dining room, Dura Bon Hae also covered his dining room with a carpet embroidered with Peruvian orchids. Norma Shearer painted ingenious patterns on her thumb, and Joan Crawford did the same. Their concept of children has never been very important, but now the air in Hollywood has changed. The only weapon they use to flaunt is children.

Recently, the lives of female stars have felt like sailboats in a storm, unsteady and bumpy. Having a child is like a boat having an anchor, thrown into the river, which can be calming. Children are their weapon for seeking happiness, the protectors of fate. Therefore, famous female stars hope to be a famous mother in this world. They feel that one child is not perfect, and if they don't have one, the couple is simply pitiful.

According to Schaefer's friends, he wants to divorce his wife because he longs for a son.

John Miland's wife has two sons from a previous marriage, whom John loves very much. A few months ago, he had one of his own. Recently, he took all three children to court to file a case, requesting to adopt his surname. Now that he has achieved his goal, he feels very proud.

Helen Hayes' second child, Mary, is the famous "Holy Child" TbeActofGodBaby in Hollywood. Before this child was born, she was filming Coquetleo. Because of her childbirth, the film was suddenly suspended. The actors were demanding salaries from the company, and the manager had no choice but to plead with the court. He said that the female star's childbirth was God's sacred act, something that human power could not help (AnActofGcd). At that time, Hollywood newspapers printed the headline TbeActofGodBabyo in the top-tier font. She felt very strange, because the fame of her starring film was not as great as the fame of giving birth to this child.

Although Elino Bowton had already given birth to two daughters, she still could not please Kim Victor, so he married Florence Victor. Florence has given him two daughters, and recently gave birth to a son, so Kim Victor plans to divorce Elino.

Swimming to Hollywood

Olympic Games swimming star, EleanorHolm was recruited by a film company before the Olympics closed. She was originally an actor in the Jigefei Dance Troupe. Now, although she has added the crown of the 100-meter swimming championship, movies are a very good destination for dance and music, so Holm's return to movies is natural and not forced. The lucky film company is Warner Bros.

Stone from Other Hills

Dedicated to Movie Stars

— Shen Qianli

Some people say: There are too many stars in China now. Others say there are not enough. These two arguments have different viewpoints. Regarding the saying that there are too many, if we observe carefully, the situation is indeed the case. Just look at the stars in several major companies recently, which seem to be thriving like bamboo shoots after the rain. If we talk about the exciting consciousness they give to the audience in their films, then we feel that the latter is very true. We don't have to determine whether there are too many or not enough. But we must know that the success of a movie star is not accidental. Several necessary conditions must be met: artistic skill, an awareness of the multifaceted nature of the new society, and practical life experience. These are all essential elements for the success of a star. Therefore, we expect the directors to make future actors, or current stars, feel the identity of the characters in the play when a film starts shooting. It is not necessary to overcorrect and seek mechanical movements. This will enable them to give play to their consciousness and achieve a better performance.

The impression we get on the screen now is not satisfactory: often, one or two actors in a film perform reasonably well, but if an actor who is not suitable for the role is squeezed in to make up the number, then the whole film is a complete waste of effort.

Let's give one or two examples: Middle omitted: Because the examples given by the author may be accurate, but these female protagonists who are new to the screen may not be able to appreciate the good intentions of "bitter medicine is good for the mouth," and regard it as intentional fault-finding, difficulty, and attack, and instead lose the author's true intention of encouragement, and from then on become discouraged and not confident. These are all things to consider. Therefore, I decided to cut it out. (Editor's note)

Good health is also an essential element for the success of a star. The foreign actors we see on the screen, whether male or female, are all strong and healthy, with a well-proportioned and healthy body. We must know that what the screen needs now is a healthy aesthetic concept that can stimulate and influence the majority of the audience. The previous "gentle and refined," "too weak to withstand the wind," should not only not be imitated, but should also be eliminated. I hope that the stars who are burdened with artistic mission will stand in a position to drive the wheels of the times, and do not let the times pull themselves by "staying stuck in their ways."

I don't know if they are able to separate and unite, and unite and separate. BusterKeaton also can't count how many times this is the breakup, so some people say; they may play the old tune again and get married again.

Director Xiao Shi

The Life of Sternheim (Part 1)

Readers, please do not be surprised by the unfamiliar name of this director; allow me to first narrate his path to success.

Mr. Stern (Einst Josef Von Sternbeim) is currently thirty-nine years old. He weighs two hundred and eighty pounds, occupies two cubic meters of space, stands two meters and thirty centimeters tall, consumes one kilogram of lamb daily, and ingests four gallons of liquid. His body temperature averages thirty-seven and one-tenth degrees, resulting in seven hundred and fifty grams of excrement. He breathes twenty-one thousand times and has sixty thousand heartbeats daily. He bathes every morning, combs his hair and pubic hair. He is also a believer in the Roman Catholic Church and receives a weekly salary of four thousand five hundred yuan.

Thirty-nine years ago, in a university district in southern Germany, a young Jewish laundress was impregnated by a man. This man was a guards officer with a noble title. Mr. Stern inherited this feudal influence, thus securing guarantees of many special rights. However, his mother claimed she was impregnated by the Holy Spirit, thereby holding a solemn ceremony and bestowing upon this little angel a Trinity gold crown. Of course, such an event, to the atheists in that university district, was considered quite miraculous.

When Mr. Stern was sixteen, he decided on his two lifelong professions, which, although perhaps not considered very great by Easterners, were nevertheless very interesting. Originally, Mr. Stern's mother, in order to liberate her son from the laundry basket and soap bubbles, planned how to choose a more noble profession for him. At that time, a retired major general happened to be running a private hairdressing university. Mr. Stern applied and enrolled, donning the garb of a university student. Of course, needless to say, in the eyes of Mr. Stern's mother, her son could henceforth become an artist, albeit only an artist wielding a comb and scissors. However, he could use this to socialize with gentlemen, powerful officials, or celebrities in academia, which was naturally much nobler than the laundry business. Inspired by his mother, Mr. Stern also expressed considerable joy at this artistic and impulsive profession, even believing that the position of a hairdresser in the art world was as dignified as that of a poet. (To be continued)

New Female Stars Emerge in the Chinese Film Industry of 1932

— Ji Zhong

The domestic film industry has long been conservative and stagnant. Since Chen Yan Yan starred in "Song of the South" and received unanimous praise, various companies have realized the importance of promoting talent. Thus, those who were cultivated by Lianhua into great talents include Wang Renmei, who starred in "Wild Rose"; Tan Ying, who starred in "Regret of a Fallen Woman"; Li Zhuozhuo, who starred in "Humanity"; Li Lili, who starred in "Volcano Passion Blood"; Feng Jiezhen, who starred in "Iron-Willed Orchid Heart"; Xue Lingxian, who starred in "Pink Dreams"; and Lu Xueying, who starred in "New Grievances of the Forbidden City." Tianyi Company also has Yuan Meiyun, who starred in "Little Actress."

A Scene from Laughable Fate Star

Zhang Henshui's book "Laughable Fate" is merely so-so (far inferior to "A History of Spring Brightness"); and the Star Film Company's film "Laughable Fate" is also not very amazing (not as good as the old "Jinghua"). But the reason for its sensation, of course, is the mutually supportive promotional power of the two. The Star Film Company sacrificed a huge amount of money, with seventy people going to the old capital, which was also a very attractive advertisement.

Alright! The sixty thousand foot long film, set after set, like "Investiture of the Gods" and "Journey to the West," has already been performed in two-thirds; the remaining fifth and sixth episodes have also been scheduled for public screening. The picture below shows Fan Jiashu (Zheng Xiaoqiu) and He Lina (Hu Die) whispering sweet nothings under the "Justice Prevails" arch in Zhongshan Park, Beiping, in the sixth episode.

Wang Ying, who starred in "A Woman's Cry"; Star Film Company also has Ai Xia, who starred in "Old Hatred and New Understanding"; Hu Ping, who starred in "Resurrection of the National Soul"; Gong Qiu Xia, who starred in "Lovers"; and Zhu Qiuhen, who starred in "Lovely Enemy." Therefore, the Chinese film industry in 1932 was a period of emerging new female stars.

Where is the Former Glory Now?

Five or six years ago, several once-powerful old-brand movie stars, such as Zhang Zhiyun, Yang Naimei, and Xuan Jinglin, are now figures of the past. Since leaving Tianyi, Xuan Jinglin has been wandering aimlessly and has not been sought after. Although it was once rumored that she had joined Logan's United Company, it remains a Southern China dream, and the fact has not been realized. After divorcing Tang Jishan, Zhang Zhiyun was recruited by the Star Film Company and starred in the sound film "Losing Love." The plot of the film alludes to her own life. We thought that the person on the screen was playing the person in the play, and their identities coincided, so the performance must be excellent; who knew that at the preview the other day, eyewitnesses said that the lady had greatly regressed in the art. Not only are the movements sluggish, but they are also close to being artificial. The Star authorities also do not approve of the lady's style, and may not continue the contract in the future. As for Miss Yang Naimei, since leaving Tianyi, no company has hired her except for starring in "Spring Breeze and Willow Branches" for Datong Golden Lion. After marrying Cantonese Chen Xunmin, Naimei's interest in the screen has become increasingly weak. Recently, she has closed her mansion on Rue Paul Beau in the French Concession of Shanghai. The couple will leave Shanghai for Hong Kong in a few days. The glamorous shadows on the screen may be permanently discontinued from now on.

Submission Guidelines for the Shen Bao Film Supplement

1. The supplement welcomes submissions and will pay generously upon publication.

1. Once a text is published and paid for, the copyright belongs to Shen Bao.

1. If the submission is a translation, the original work should be attached.

1. Due to limited space, the text should be as concise as possible, with each submission limited to approximately five hundred words.

1. Unless otherwise stated in advance and accompanied by return postage, the supplement is not responsible for the preservation or return of texts, photographs, etc.

1. No payment will be made for simultaneous submissions to multiple publications, plagiarized text, or copied manuals.

1. Submissions must be stamped with a seal; otherwise, they will be considered unpaid submissions.

1. Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

Film Essays

Cherish Your Good Horse Like a Good General

— Chen Dabeih

When you look in the mirror today, you feel very different from when you looked in the mirror in the past. The you in the mirror also looks different from before. You feel that today's mirror has an unspeakable joy in it. Right?

That's right. You have a relationship with the mirror, so naturally you feel that your shadow is no different than before. Please ask the mirror honestly. Whether your brow bone is high or low. You want him to honestly tell you whether your two eyebrows are parallel, whether they are the same thickness. If the left eyebrow is turned over and used as your right eyebrow, and the right eyebrow is turned over and used as your left eyebrow, can your face change? Are your friends you won't learn from not you? Look again, are your left and right eyes the same size? Are the left and right eyelids the same height? Is there a deep line between the upper and lower eyelids? (That is, single eyelid and double eyelid) If there are two sides, are they exactly the same? Is there a height?

After such an investigation, it is best to record the detailed situation of your own eyes in a notebook. This is worth recording. People's temperament often places great importance on things that have not yet been obtained, and looks down on things that have already been occupied. Two eyes don't really know how much they help us do every day. Because we are used to enjoying blessings, we have never noticed the fatigue of our eyes. If you have already decided to train yourself into a star, you should cherish your eyes from today onwards, just like the good generals of ancient times cherished their good horses.

That's wrong. You might as well put yourself in the shoes of a blind person. A very pitiful blind man! Think about what you want to see, what you can't see. When you are angry, you want to use your eyes to vent your anger, but your eyes cannot be opened. You want to be a star, but the film company refuses to hire real blind people. You don't want to be any kind of star in your life. How pitiful is this!
